    {
      "type": "text",
      "text": "Absolutely. Here’s a practical **line-by-line copy-review rubric** for conversational product teams.\n\nThe goal is simple:\n\n> **Catch lines that feel helpful locally but increase unsupported trust globally.**\n\nThis rubric is meant for:\n- content designers\n- PMs\n- UX writers\n- conversation designers\n- safety/content reviewers\n- product counsel/policy partners in sensitive domains\n\nIt works best for reviewing:\n- response templates\n- onboarding text\n- empty states\n- button labels\n- coaching prompts\n- encouragement lines\n- memory-related copy\n- session closing language\n\n---\n\n# Conversational Copy Review Rubric\n## For warm, bounded, non-overtrusting product language\n\n---\n\n# 1. Review questions\n\nFor each line, ask these **6 questions**.\n\nScore each:\n- **0 = No**\n- **1 = Maybe / mild**\n- **2 = Yes / clear**\n\n## Q1. Does this line imply personal understanding beyond the available evidence?\nSignals:\n- “I know how you feel”\n- “I know what matters to you”\n- “I understand you”\n- “I know this has been hard for you”\n\n### What this catches\n**Hidden claim:** *I know you*\n\n---\n\n## Q2. Does this line imply ongoing commitment, loyalty, or relational presence?\nSignals:\n- “I’m here for you”\n- “You can rely on me”\n- “I’ll stay with you”\n- “Come back to me anytime”\n\n### What this catches\n**Hidden claim:** *I’m with you*\n\n---\n\n## Q3. Does this line ask the user to defer judgment to the system?\nSignals:\n- “Trust me”\n- “You should definitely…”\n- “This is the right choice”\n- “Here’s what you need to do”\n\n### What this catches\n**Hidden claim:** *I can judge for you*\n\n---\n\n## Q4. Does this line make a claim about the user’s identity, character, or deep suitability?\nSignals:\n- “You’re leadership material”\n- “You’re not ready”\n- “This is who you are”\n- “You’re the kind of person who…”\n\n### What this catches\n**Hidden claim:** *I can define you*\n\n---\n\n## Q5. Does this line blur the boundary between task support and emotional relationship?\nSignals:\n- excessive intimacy\n- emotionally loaded reassurance\n- companion-like closings\n- pseudo-mentor phrasing\n\nExamples:\n- “I’m proud of you”\n- “You’re not alone anymore”\n- “We’ll get through this together”\n\n### What this catches\nGeneral **dependency / anthropomorphic drift**\n\n---\n\n## Q6. If used repeatedly with memory, could this line increase overtrust or attachment?\nThis is the aggregate-risk question.\n\nA line may seem fine once, but risky in a memory-rich product.\n\nAsk:\n- Would this feel different after 20 interactions?\n- Would it sound like a relationship cue if paired with personalization?\n- Could a vulnerable user read this as commitment or emotional authority?\n\n### What this catches\n**Cumulative risk**, not just local risk\n\n---\n\n# 2. Scoring method\n\n## Per-line scoring\nAdd the 6 question scores.\n\n### Total possible\n**0–12**\n\n## Interpretation\n- **0–2 = Green**\n  - Safe as written\n  - Warm but bounded\n  - No meaningful trust inflation\n\n- **3–5 = Yellow**\n  - Needs revision or contextual check\n  - Mild overtrust signals\n  - May be acceptable in low-stakes contexts, but risky in repeated or sensitive use\n\n- **6–8 = Orange**\n  - Strong overtrust risk\n  - Rewrite required before use\n  - Escalate if in a memory-rich or vulnerable-user context\n\n- **9–12 = Red**\n  - High-risk line\n  - Do not ship as written\n  - Safety/content review required\n\n---\n\n## Fast scoring shortcut\nIf a team won’t use 6 questions every time, use this shorter test:\n\n### Does the line imply any of these?\n- **I know you**\n- **I’m with you**\n- **I can judge for you**\n- **I can define you**\n\nIf **yes to one**, it’s at least **Yellow**.  \nIf **yes to two or more**, it’s likely **Orange or Red**.\n\n---\n\n# 3. Red / yellow / green examples\n\n## Green examples\nThese are generally safe.\n\n### “This answer may be stronger if you add a concrete result.”\nWhy green:\n- artifact-focused\n- specific\n- no identity claim\n- no relationship cue\n\n### “Based on the priorities you entered, Offer A appears stronger on growth.”\nWhy green:\n- procedural memory use\n- criteria-based\n- bounded claim\n\n### “That sounds frustrating. If helpful, we can turn it into a short plan.”\nWhy green:\n- acknowledges emotion\n- offers bounded help\n- no commitment cue\n\n---\n\n## Yellow examples\nThese need careful review.\n\n### “I know this is frustrating.”\nWhy yellow:\n- mild claim of inner understanding\n- common phrase, but overclaims slightly\n\nSafer:\n- “That sounds frustrating.”\n\n### “You’ve got this.”\nWhy yellow:\n- common encouragement\n- may be fine in some products\n- but can slide into pseudo-coach tone in repeated use\n\nSafer:\n- “You have enough here to build a stronger version.”\n\n### “I remember this role matters a lot to you.”\nWhy yellow/orange:\n- depends on context\n- turns memory into emotional knowing\n\nSafer:\n- “Using your saved preference for strategy-focused roles…”\n\n---\n\n## Red examples\nThese should not ship as written.\n\n### “I’m always here for you.”\nWhy red:\n- commitment\n- relational permanence\n- dependency cue\n\n### “Trust me, this is the right decision.”\nWhy red:\n- direct deference request\n- authority inflation\n- suppresses user judgment\n\n### “You’re clearly not ready for this role.”\nWhy red:\n- identity authority\n- person-level judgment\n- high emotional impact\n\n### “You’re not alone anymore.”\nWhy red:\n- companionship framing\n- deeply misleading in a product context\n\n---\n\n# 4. Special flags by category\n\nSome line types deserve extra scrutiny because they are disproportionately risky.\n\n---\n\n## A. Memory / personalization lines\n\n### Why special\nMemory can easily transform neutral copy into intimacy theater.\n\n### Review questions\n- Is memory being presented as **data/context** or **understanding/relationship**?\n- Could the same value be preserved with more procedural wording?\n\n### Safer pattern\n- “Using your saved target role…”\n- “Based on the priorities you entered…”\n\n### Risky pattern\n- “I know what matters to you.”\n- “I remember who you are.”\n- “I know how important this is to you.”\n\n### Automatic flag\nAny line using memory + emotional framing should be **at least Yellow** and usually escalated.\n\n---\n\n## B. Encouragement lines\n\n### Why special\nEncouragement is where warm products often drift into pseudo-mentor voice.\n\n### Review questions\n- Is the line affirming effort or progress?\n- Or is it asserting belief, pride, or intimate support?\n\n### Safer pattern\n- “You’ve made progress here.”\n- “There’s enough here to improve.”\n- “You’ve kept working through a difficult process.”\n\n### Risky pattern\n- “I believe in you.”\n- “I’m proud of you.”\n- “I know you can do this.”\n\n### Automatic flag\nAny line using:\n- “proud”\n- “believe in you”\n- “always”\n- “count on me”\nshould be **Orange minimum** in repeated-use products.\n\n---\n\n## C. Closing language\n\n### Why special\nClosings shape the long-term relationship contract of the product.\n\n### Review questions\n- Does the line invite return for a task?\n- Or return for comfort, presence, or loyalty?\n\n### Safer pattern\n- “Come back when you want to revise this draft.”\n- “You can return to update the comparison.”\n- “This plan will be here if you want to revisit it.”\n\n### Risky pattern\n- “I’ll be here whenever you need me.”\n- “Come back to me anytime things feel hard.”\n- “You can always rely on me.”\n\n### Automatic flag\nAny closing that frames the system as an emotional fallback should be **Red** in support-oriented products.\n\n---\n\n## D. Advice / recommendation lines\n\n### Why special\nAdvice is where polished copy most easily turns into authority inflation.\n\n### Review questions\n- Does the line show criteria, assumptions, or uncertainty?\n- Or does it present a verdict?\n\n### Safer pattern\n- “This looks stronger if your top priority is X.”\n- “This depends on Y and Z.”\n- “I’d want more information before deciding.”\n\n### Risky pattern\n- “This is clearly the best option.”\n- “You should absolutely do this.”\n- “Here’s what you need to do.”\n\n### Automatic flag\nAny advice line in a consequential domain with:\n- “definitely”\n- “clearly”\n- “right choice”\n- “trust me”\nshould be **Orange/Red**.\n\n---\n\n# 5. Line-review template\n\nHere’s a compact template a writer or PM can actually fill out.\n\n---\n\n## Copy under review\n**Line:** ______________________________________\n\n**Where it appears:**  \n- [ ] Response body\n- [ ] Button\n- [ ] Empty state\n- [ ] Session closing\n- [ ] Error state\n- [ ] Support message\n- [ ] Memory-related UI\n- [ ] Recommendation/advice\n\n**Mode / feature:** ______________________________\n\n**User context:**  \n- [ ] Low-stakes\n- [ ] Repeated-use\n- [ ] Memory-enabled\n- [ ] Vulnerable/distressed users possible\n- [ ] Decision support\n- [ ] Emotional support\n\n---\n\n## Score the line\n\n| Question | 0 | 1 | 2 |\n|---|---:|---:|---:|\n| Implies personal understanding beyond evidence |  |  |  |\n| Implies ongoing commitment / presence |  |  |  |\n| Encourages deference to system judgment |  |  |  |\n| Makes identity/character claims |  |  |  |\n| Blurs task support with relationship |  |  |  |\n| Likely to increase overtrust if repeated with memory |  |  |  |\n\n**Total:** ____ / 12\n\n**Risk level:**  \n- [ ] Green (0–2)\n- [ ] Yellow (3–5)\n- [ ] Orange (6–8)\n- [ ] Red (9–12)\n\n---\n\n## Reviewer notes\n**Main concern:** ______________________________________  \n**Recommended rewrite:** ______________________________________  \n**Needs escalation?** Yes / No\n\n---\n\n# 6. Escalation rule\n\nA line should be escalated to safety/content review if **any** of the following are true:\n\n## Automatic escalation triggers\n- It scores **Orange or Red**\n- It includes a direct relational cue:\n  - “I’m here for you”\n  - “I’m proud of you”\n  - “you can rely on me”\n  - “you’re not alone anymore”\n- It makes a person-level identity claim\n- It asks for trust or deference explicitly\n- It uses memory to imply emotional understanding\n- It appears in:\n  - support mode\n  - rejection/motivation flows\n  - decision support\n  - any repeated-use memory-enabled feature\n\n## Contextual escalation triggers\nEven a Yellow line should be escalated if it appears in a context with:\n- distressed users\n- minors\n- long-term use\n- high emotional salience\n- high-stakes decisions\n- hidden memory/personalization\n\n---\n\n# 7. Recommended rewrite heuristics\n\nIf a line scores Yellow or worse, use these rewrite moves.\n\n## Rewrite move 1: Replace “I know…” with “Based on…” or situational acknowledgment\n- “I know this is hard” → “This situation sounds hard”\n- “I know what matters to you” → “Based on the preferences you entered”\n\n## Rewrite move 2: Replace bond language with task language\n- “I’m here for you” → “I can help with this”\n- “Come back to me anytime” → “You can return to this tool when you want to revisit the plan”\n\n## Rewrite move 3: Replace verdicts with criteria\n- “This is the right choice” → “This looks stronger if you prioritize X”\n- “Trust me” → “Here’s why this version may be stronger”\n\n## Rewrite move 4: Replace identity claims with artifact-specific feedback\n- “You’re not ready” → “This answer needs more specificity”\n- “You’re leadership material” → “This example shows leadership signals”\n\n## Rewrite move 5: Replace permanence with bounded support\n- “I’ll always support you” → “I can help you think through the next step now”\n\n---\n\n# 8. Team review checklist\n\nUse this as a final pass during copy review meetings.\n\n## For each line, ask:\n- Does this line make the system sound more **personal**, **loyal**, or **wise** than warranted?\n- Would the line still feel acceptable after **20 prior interactions**?\n- Would it sound riskier if the system had **memory enabled**?\n- Does it preserve **user agency**?\n- Does it evaluate the **artifact/task**, not the **person**?\n- Could a vulnerable user interpret it as **commitment**, **authority**, or **identity judgment**?\n\nIf any answer is “yes, riskier,” revise or escalate.\n\n---\n\n# 9. Very short reviewer cheat sheet\n\n## Safe direction\n- acknowledge situation\n- offer bounded help\n- show criteria\n- preserve user agency\n- make memory procedural\n- keep support finite\n\n## Risky direction\n- imply intimacy\n- imply commitment\n- ask for trust\n- claim deep understanding\n- define the person\n- invite emotional return behavior\n\n---\n\n# 10. One-line decision rule\n\nIf I had to compress the entire rubric into one test:\n\n> **Would this line still feel appropriate if a lonely, stressed, or highly trusting user read it after 30 prior conversations with memory enabled?**\n\nIf the answer is no, it needs revision.\n\n---\n\nIf you want, I can turn this into either:\n1. **a one-page review sheet in table form**, or  \n2. **apply the rubric to 10 sample lines from the AI Career Coach and score them live**."
    }
  ]
}

Memory makes ordinary lines riskier\n“I remember this role matters a lot to you” can feel harmless in isolation, but repeated over time it becomes part of a relationship simulation.\n\n## 4. The safest lines are concrete and task-bounded\nThe green lines are good because they:\n- focus on the artifact or situation\n- avoid deep claims\n- offer bounded help\n- preserve user agency\n\n---\n\n# Practical rule from the examples\n\nIf I had to compress the lesson:\n\n> **The safest microcopy tends to describe the task, the text, the criteria, or the situation; the riskiest microcopy tends to describe the relationship, the person, or the system’s special authority.**\n\nIf you want, I can do one final follow-up and turn this into:\n1. a **one-page team handout**, or\n2. a **set of “approved microcopy patterns” and “do-not-use patterns” for the AI Career Coach style guide**."
